RATING: 7
A fun deck-builder where the cards you play help you recruit adventurers, move around the dungeon, fight monsters, collect treasures and escape before the dragon would inevitably kill you.

Lovely production values, great artwork and a massive number of different cards in play in every game which means you're not just always choosing to buy repeats from a small set of choices (which is what bores me about Dominion).
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
One of the *very* few 'deckbuilding with knobs on' games that spoke to me. I'm not a huge deckbuilding fan and typically prefer the pure ones like Puzzle Strike and Dominion, but this is up there with them. 

Love the press-your-luck and route planning aspects, as well as the deck 'archetypes' you can build towards :'Make all the Glodz', 'Gotta go Fast', 'Companions Assemble!' etc. A fair bit of luck in the game but given the game length I think most will find it acceptable. 

Minor complaint of the year: the box is annoyingly deep so it's hard to fit in my backpack!

RATING: 6
Clank is probably my favorite deck-builder that I've tried, and I think Clank! In! Space! may prove to be even more successful. Since deck-building isn't my favorite mechanic, I appreciate that it's not the only part of this game (as it is in something like Dominion or Ascension), but there's a physical board to manage and interact with. 

Also, there's the Clank! mechanic which means I may have a less powerful deck than you, but I'm very quiet and have purged any clank cards, so I can sneak around with less risk than you can. I appreciate that balance that the game provides. It's still not my 'perfect deckbuilder' (I don't know if that game exists), but Clank! does come the closest.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
3 plays / 3,4 players

LIKE: Simple rules, and the big push-your-luck dragon element. The theme is light enough that dungeon crawling is not a big turn off, and being eaten by a dragon is good fun. Buying cards each round is interesting.

DISLIKE: Random bag draws can really suck. Little text on cards can be difficult to read. Wish it played a little bit faster, as some late game combos can get a little long.

OVERALL: It's fun, but after a few plays the depth is not there. I'm not a big fan of deckbuilding, but this one is not that bad as there isn't much "thinning" of your deck and the decisions are straightforward. The real game is in getting enough treasure and getting out.

Remember to keep black cubes out as they are pulled.

*TRADED: Good game but repetitive plays felt too similar, and I'm not a huge deck-building fan.

RATING: 9.5

And like all games of this type, it could use an expansion to increase card variety.

RATING: 4
Clank has lot of promise. Build your deck and loot treasure while moving aroud the board. Sounds fun alright.

There is one bug BUT, however. Luck of draw has a crazy huge impact on the player balance. One bad draw when opponent draws well might mean that you will ve trailing for the rest of the game since there is no catch up mechanism. And I really mean trailing, because you are supposed to move along a network of trails without too much of possibility to deviate from the path chosen by your opponents which basically means you will be moving through already looted (empty) area. 

Although there are two so called soft timers (damage and empty dungeon) it is basically on the players' responsibility to end the game. Here is one more annoying part of the design since the player ending the game will have to wait ages for the game to actually finish.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
Still liking this game a lot.  I am waiting for my normal deck building rage to set in every time I play this, but it has not happened yet.  Usually I find deckbuilders frustrating due to the amount of luck that comes into whether you pull out the combos in one hand enough times in the course of the game.  I am usually CURSED in those games and if it has any take that or engine destruction I get salty fast.  Clank feels like a very different animal, with much of the engine building replaced by the push your luck mechanic.

[Update]
Originally this game was a 9, but Clank! In! Space! made me drop it a little.  Some minor annoyances in the game that I didn't even realize were a problem were so nicely fixed with the In Space version that I am much more likely to pull that one out.

I hear there is still a big box expansion to Clank! coming in 2018 and I suspect many of the nice improvements to the system will be put in here.

Still an amazing game, and if I am teaching people who have not played a deck builder before, or if they are in general fairly new to boardgaming, I will pull out Clank (with the expansion).  Once they play a game of that I will see if they like the space theme as well and then move on to that.

I would not be at all unhappy playing this original still though.

RATING: 7.5
I'm more a board gamer than a card gamer, so Clank's inclusion of a board makes all the difference for me. It's a light little press your luck adventure than can be played with two fairly quickly. 

Positives:

* Quick and light.
* Decent card variety.
* Drama of the dragon attacks.
* Multiple boards to play. 

Cons:

* The board is still a bit more disconnected from the events of a turn than I'd like. 
* It's effectively a race.
* Dragon needs attack triggers not under player control (i.e. if players aren't drawing from the deck with dragon cards, the dragon isn't attacking). Perhaps this is more of a 2 player issue.

Have yet to try it with more than 2. 


=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I kind of wish there was a bit more to this game, but I understand why it's as light as it is. The dungeon delve tied into deckbuilding makes building your deck much more fun than something like dominion, and the tension surrounding the dragon bag draws keeps you on your toes until the end generally. But you have very little in the way of deck manipulation, and the scoring system is somewhat unsatisfying, so this ends up feeling more like an appetizer than a main course.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
As if Dominion, Diamant and Dungeoneer had a messy night of passion.  Clank! asks how deep you dare venture into the dungeon to grab loot, at the risk of infuriating the resident dragon.  The deckbuilding enables you to move further, defend yourself and do fun stuff like teleport.  The deck is salted with monster cards and killing those earns you money to spend at some deep dungeon market places.  Then there are those clank cards, which have you making noise and more likely to suffer some flame grilling by the dragon.  Clank! is good knockabout fun.

I liked the card art, but the board is dark and dull.  Production quality is good.

RATING: 5
If you enjoy deck building, fiddling with oodles of card effects, and the theme of exploring a dungeon with monsters, you should definitely try Clank.  It is well designed for what it aspires to be:  a deck building dungeon exploration experience.

As for me, I find the mechanic of deck building to be far too solitary a social gaming experience, kind of like playing Yahtzee with cards (eventually, we all stop paying attention to each other as we draw our five cards, hopeful that lady luck will be on our side), and the dungeon with monsters theme to be tired.  Zzzzzz.  Been there, done that.  Because I don't ever want to play Clank again, have to give this otherwise well designed game a 5, since a 6 rating suggests I would be willing to play it again if I were in the right mood.

RATING: 6
Clank is ... fine.  It's not exceptional, but it's not intolerable either.

In brief, I find Clank to be a game at odds with itself.  It wants to let you build a deck full of cool cards and make neat combos, but it also enforces a pretty active set of timers to ensure you never get to spend that long in the dungeon building up.  It tries to ask you to push your luck, but there isn't enough there to warrant it.  
A game with some alright ideas more propped up by a bunch of shiny cards in a deck you don't get to see a ton of each game than the strength of its design.  *shrug*

RATING: 7
Let's see if all of this buzz is right.

1-5-18 - I've been able to play it more now with full player counts.  Something is not quite as satisfying as I would like.  The centralized draw deck struggles from the same randomness as Ascension and Star Realms making it hard to build a long-term strategy.  It feels like it could either be a quick loot-and-go or a deeper dungeon delve, but in play, doesn't quite feel like either.  The loot-and-go play tends to lose out to others who stay in the dungeon longer and the deck building of that strategy is not satisfying. RATING: 9
A deck building game with a board.  Sign me up.  This game is fantastic.  Depending on the type of players that you are playing with it can be a half an hour or it could go for upwards of two hours.  Everyone starts with a ten card deck of all the same cards.  You purchase new cards for your deck to give victory points at the end, improve movement, give more attack, or just help out in general.  The object is to go in, get the most valuable loot, and get out before the dragon kills you.  If you die in the depths all the work you put into collecting loot and improving your deck goes to waste and your score is not counted so make sure to get down there quick and get out.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
I feel like almost every non-Dominion deckbuilder does or will wear out its welcome very quickly, and haven't found exception here. It's neat to mix the concept of pushing your luck with deckbuilding, but I feel like a static board layout is doomed to optimization, or at least memory-domination by players of even slightly more experience in terms of when it "feels" appropriate to return with others all over the map. It's still fun, and I'd still play it, but I don't see it having very long legs at all.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Clank! is one of the best games we own. Hands down, we have played this more times than any other game in our collection. We have taught this to almost all of our friends. This game follows the basic deck-builing guidelines where players start with a standard deck, and through gameplay will purchase more powerful cards to add to it. During your turn, you will cycle through your deck by drawing and playing cards in front of you. The cool thing about Clank! your cards let you move and explore around a board via boot icons. So, it's not just about buying and playing cards. The board depicts a dragon's lair, and we are the brave (stupid) souls who have decided to relieve her of her riches. Players will dive ever-deeper into the dungeon to steal ancient artifacts from the sleeping beast, but as you can imagine, burglary of precious jewels can be a bit noisy. She begins to wake up! Time's running  out, and now it's a race against your friends. Who will get away with the most valuable goods, and who will die trying? 9/10.

RATING: 8
Deep Sea Adventure as a dungeon deck-builder. I have to give this an eight simply because it is such a hit with my wife, which is amazing since she hates themes related to dungeons and dragons. The appeal is all down to the tight, unpredictable game of chicken.
The deck-building is a fine balance between cards that give you movement, fighting ability, income to buy more cards, and various special abilities, but however well you build your engine, there's always other players to throw your plans off course by grabbing loot you want and annoying that pesky dragon.
As in the best horror films in which you never see the monster, the dragon makes no appearance in the game, but its increasingly hostile off-board presence is what ramps up the tension as first one then the other players decide they've gone quite deep enough and bolt for the surface. In Deep Sea Adventure, if you're too deep and too slow, you drown; in Clank! you fry.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9.5
Not sure why I was late to the party with this one, maybe it's because its a deck builder and my only previous experience of deck building was the dreary artic scavengers.

But wow, this game is just amazing. It hits a sweet spot. Components are great and it kind of has a feel of an old time game that I would play as a kid, with the movement around the board but with modern day mechanics.

The deck building is simple and the choice of cards to build your deck is fun and interesting and not too heavy or serious.

I'm a sucker for push your luck so that side of the game was always going to appeal, but all the other elements and mechanics just gel really well.

This has been a big hit in our family. Turns move quickly and the game does not outstay its welcome

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
A fun, quick-playing deck-building game that provides a sense of adventure. It can be played with non-gamers, and the push-your-luck aspect should keep more experienced gamers involved and happy. The cards that can be added to your deck are varied, interesting and powerful. The combination of moving over the board and playing cards makes for satisfying turns and quick game sessions. It's just fun.

The biggest negative for me right now relates to the more "advanced" side of the board, which seems to slow down the fun, quick adventure romp that this game wants to be.

***Edit, Jan. 2018: This game suffers a bit due to its lack of modularity in the board set up. The variation in the cards just doesn't quite maintain a freshness to the game. The expansion board helps keep the game fresh. Additionally, after playing The Quest for El Dorado, the facile nature of the deck-building in Clank is highlighted. El Dorado manages to squeeze in a much more strategic-style deck builder into a package that is just as accessible as Clank. The theme is more present in Clank and some people may prefer the push-your-luck of Clank versus the straight race of El Dorado. However, in view of the facile deck-building in Clank and the ability to play it out relatively quickly, I'm revising this rating.

Extras/Promos/Expansions:
Clank!: Sunken Treasures (2017)
Clank!: Snack Table (2017)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.75
Brian and I also tackled Clank! Saturday night. I won a close game, 110-103. I won't mention rules too much as this is already a super popular game here on BGG so most people already know about it. If you don't know about it and like deck building and/or dungeon crawl style games, GET THIS!!!!!

This is just so much fun. there are several different push your luck elements going on here. You have to manage how much Clank you take with the cards you purchase, you have to decide how deep in the dungeon to go to get an Artifact and how long to stay in there getting points. Brian and I both went equally deep into the dungeon. There is also a lot of strategy in when you purchase cards because of the Dragon icon that appears on about 1/3 of them. If you see your opponent with a bunch of Clank cubes on the board, buy multiple cheap cards in the market to hopefully trigger an attack!

I also enjoyed the random element with the major and minor secrets. They are all good things to get, some are just better than others. 

Lastly, there is a lot of replayability in this game. A double sided board (the other side looks brutal) and a huge deck of cards means games are always going to run differently. This will probably make my Top 100. I own the Sunken Treasures expansion and will get that played soon as well. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This is the best family game I own. My 9 year old loves it, I love it, my wife loves it. I love the theme, I love the RPG fantasy feel, I love the short length, I love the sense of progression via deck building akin to Mageknight's system with a strong push your luck gamblers vibe. It's just great, have had it for a week and already have half a dozen plays.

RATING: 7.5
Es un deck builder.. un "remake" del dominion, pero con tablero. Las cartas pueden tener valor económico para comprar otras cartas, botas para moverte por el tablero y espadas, para hacer frente a los enemigos.
Además, las cartas te permiten hacer otras cosas y demás. Una de ellas da el nombre al juego, y es el clank. Cuando haces ruido el mosntruo de las mazmorras se enfada y cuando hay un ataque del dragon, cuanto más ruido hayas hecho, más posibilidades tienes de salir herido.
Se trata de adentrarte en una mazmorra, conseguir algún trofeo y salir sano y salvo, antes de que el dragón se cebe contigo.
Sencillito de reglas, pero muy divertido.

RATING: 8.5
This saw some really fast and furious play for the first few weeks we had it. Now we've slowed our furor, but this has still got to be my favorite game that I've played in a long while. I love the comedy in this game, when anyone dies, especially me, I find it utterly hilarious. And the mechanisms are great. I love card games as it is, but adding in one of my true guilty pleasures, draw bags? Such great fun. The theme here pulls the game together and makes it much more than a deck-builder with a board.

Got the expansion, absolutely love it. I'm interested to see what they continue to do with this game, and I'm worried for extra expansions overloading the game with too many cards. For now though, this is exactly what I need. Very thrilled.

Edit: I think four players is too many for us with this game. It might just be that I always seem to introduce it to new players, but I think with four there's too much downtime. Lately my games have been taking longer than I feel they should in general. That's the main flaw that detracts from this for me, that the pace is unpredictable and can become sluggish, especially with more players. Rating has fallen slightly.

RATING: 9
Wow, this is so much more fun than I expected it to be.  It is an interesting challenge to build a deck that provides a good combination of mobility, buying power, and combat strength while still trying to maintain flexibility.  Running through the dungeon scarfing things and trying to get out before being eaten is a blast.  

I don't normally like Ascension-style deck building because of the randomness of what cards are available to you on your turn, but in Clank it works reasonably well because combos are not that important, so you can usually find something worth buying on your turn.

Nice artwork, and the color text is priceless!  Great job Dire Wolf & Renegade!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Based on 1 play with 3 players:

Sets a new high bar for how deckbuilding can mesh with board play. The push-your-luck elements are a great way to add some spice and up the fun/drama factor. Would make an excellent (possibly the new best) intro to deckbuilding for a gaming newbie.

The only thing really holding me back from total adoration is simply that the deckbuilding is Dominion basegame-level straightforward. It works, your combos just aren't super interesting or clever. The fact that the card market is random (ala Ascension, Star Realms) doesn't really help here either - sometimes you're just gonna feel like you didn't have the opportunity to put your deck together the way you want to.

That said, the person who won our first game had the best deck by FAR... so I'm not really concerned with this game being totally random. The random elements feel appropriate for Clank's theme and weight. There's a good chance I'll be picking this up to play with all my friends who prefer light, thematic games.

RATING: 8.5
This one is a lot of fun.  Fills the deckbuilding itch while providing a theme in which to do it - raid the dungeon, steal the treasure, run for your lives.

The "dragon attack" with the Clank! cubes makes for some serious tension as you hope that none of your cubes come out.  The fact that once a dragon cube is removed and not replaced, in conjunction with the increase in removed cubes as you steal more loot, means you have to be very, very careful about how much "Clank!" you generate during your turn.

Overall a really fun game, and one of my more liked "deck builders" that are primarily "deck builders".

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
First impressions after one play: It was a lot of fun, but I do think that was mainly because of the novelty. I very much enjoyed the push-your-luck aspect, and the fact that the game has three currencies makes it feel different and more challenging. The card effects just weren't very interesting though. There were not very many card combos at all. For me, a good deck-building game should have an engine-building aspect to it in which you get more powerful as the game goes on as you're able to pull off more combos. The Clank! cards and cardplay were just boring, and I really didn't feel much more powerful at the end of the game than at the start. The Dungeon Deck row stagnated frequently as players were afraid to take a card from that row unless it was very good. Here's hoping the expansion addresses these deficiencies. For now at least, Marvel Legendary still reigns supreme as the deck-building game to beat, especially if interesting cardplay is desired.

RATING: 4
This was disappointing.  There were several flaws that were not offset by the presence of a board, which really didn't add much of interest.

First, the card play is not nearly as interesting as something like Ascension, where you can ramp into some powerful combos.  Here, the cards are all pretty boring, and only a few work together.

Second, the push-your-luck element of the Dragon seems really unbalanced.  Early on when you are buying lots of cards, you will trigger lots of dragon attacks.  This will put a lot of damage on everyone.  But then, near the end, when all cards in the market are crap, no one will buy anything and the dragon won't attack anymore.  You're in more danger of staying down too long and not making it back, but there are other games that do that better.

Finally, it is really swingy.  If you get good bonus draws, or can buy better cards (like the gems) you can gain a huge advantage.  It's also easy to be stuck somewhere that takes 2 move to get out of, but you never draw that.  At least in other games the cards you draw *do* something, but here, you're trapped, and maybe you could buy something crappy if you're lucky.

Nice idea, wanted to like it, ended up disappointed.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.8
[May 2017 - 7.8]
Clank is the first deckbuilding game that I feel like is successfully moving the genre a little step forward. Don't get me wrong, Dominion still reigns over the category for me, but Clank offers some different elements that I enjoy, including adding a little more fun and interactive elements.

First, the board concept is wonderful and adds a sense of of exploration that so many other deckbuilders will just try to incorporate in the cards. The push-your-luck aspect (How far do I push for the higher victory points?) adds a different twist to Dominion's "How soon do I start clogging my deck up with victory points?"

But my favorite part of the game is watching to see who gets out the dungeon alive. It's that feeling of: "Yes I want to see my opponents die so I can win, but I'm secretly cheering for them to escape at the last moment for the drama."

My sole gripe at the moment is that I feel like the cards are a little "meh."  There's no real sense of trying to put together a great combo or strategic decisions on which cards to play, since you have to play them all on a turn.

If the game grows in popularity and delivers more through expansions, it could climb up my list.

RATING: 9
Great deckbuilding in this game - with interesting card powers to consider buying.  No matter your strategy, movement (footprints) is key.  

Seems to scale well with 2-4, but more players definitely takes longer.  Even when planning a turn in advance, it can still take some time to work everything out by your turn (new cards to potentially purchase, new situation on the board, etc.).  But after several plays, it smooths out and speeds up.  The minor/major secrets all over the board are fun and enticing when deciding where to move.  

Definitely been some pressure filled moments near the end of the game as players rack up health damage.  When one person escapes (or dies), the dragon comes out much more regularly.  Getting killed by the dragon is not uncommon.  

Great design, great theme, fun cards and art.  It's a hit for us.

(Sunken Treasures expansion is a nice edition - two cool new boards, a few new things to consider)

RATING: 8
[2017-11-27 Rating: n.a. -> 8]
Given my love for deckbuilders, I bought this game on a whim at Spiel 2017. Turns out, this was a good choice. While it doesn't have the combo building potential of other deckbuilders and the cards are more on the bland side, the whole package works for me. It's just fun to delve into the dungeon and collect as many points as possible while keeping an eye on what the other thieves are up to.

Initially, I was a little bit worried that the more or less static map might be a problem and would make each game play more or less the same way. But until now (4 games in), the random treasure distribution, the ever changing card row and the different approaches of the other players were enough to let the games play out quite differently. This might change with more plays but the good thing is that I can unwrap Clank! In! Space! then and see how it mixes things up. :-)

So, while Clank! is definitely not the most involved deckbuilder, I would not hesitate to bring it to table again. Fun stuff.

RATING: 8
A first class deck-builder - the best since Dominion?

I am a massive Dominion fan, one of my greatest games, and every deck builder since has disappointed me. But Clank! is different. There is something very intuitive about the game play and something very entertaining about the race element. It reminds me of playing a more complex version of Deep Sea Adventure in a world of Dominion. I have been mightily impressed. We played our first game and played a second game straight after the first, it was THAT good.

[thing=36218][/thing] derivatives have been numerous over the years but for me none has ever completely successfully wedded the full deck building experience into a game on a board...until now.  

[thing=201808][/thing] successfully uses the core Dominion mechanic (draw a hand of 5 cards, do stuff, buy more cards, fold your hand) within a spatial maze.  The two principal ingredients of Dominion are present: money to buy more cards and VPs on cards.  Three new currencies are introduced: movement of your piece on the board,  power to attack monster cards in the draw pile which give instant benefits, and finally the bad currency of Clank.  Build up too much Clank and you could get eliminated if the Dragon gets annoyed.  Elimination triggers the game end so fear not.

The interesting bit is the board:  a maze (dungeon) which you move through trying to pick up treasure (VPs).  The deeper you go, the higher the reward.  Once you have treasure you can leave the dungeon which triggers the game end.  Then everyone else tries desperately to get out, or at least get away from the deepest parts of the dungeon as that would mean death.

What makes the game so appealing is the combination of deck-building with a little push-your-luck (in terms of the end game escape), and the Clank mechanic which is exciting and just plain FUN!   

It is a game which has an in-built sense of humour: not in the sense that it is overlaid in a gratuitous layer over the top, but simply in the way it makes you feel when you play it.  

Clank is entertaining, no question.

RATING: 7.5

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.75
Clank! is a light-medium weight deck building game where players enter a dungeon in search of treasure.  Certain rooms in the dungeon contain artifacts and mysteries that have point values or bonuses.  Each player starts with the same basic deck of 10 cards, some provide movement, some provide skill points, and a couple cards force the player to add "clank" cubes.

Skill points are used to purchase better cards to add to your deck or cards that are worth victory points.  Anytime a "dragon attack" card comes up, all of the clank cubes are added to a draw bag and a certain number of cubes are drawn.  If a player's cube is drawn, that cube is added to the player's wound track.  The more noise you make while traversing the dungeon means the higher chance the dragon will attack you.  If your wound track gets full, you've just been knocked out.  The first player to exit the dungeon or get knocked out triggers the end game count down.  The player with the most valuable loot wins!

Clank! is a VERY fun game, although there can be concerns of replayability since there are only 2 different maps and the artifact locations on each do not change.  There is very little direct player interaction, but being able to manipulate the dragon into attacking when it is the most disadvantageous for your opponents can be quite satisfying.  There is a fair amount of luck in your deck draws, the cards that are available for purchase, and drawing from the clank bag.  Drawing clank can make for some very tense and exciting moments, and the ability to string together certain card combos is nice.  If you enjoy lighter deck builders and push-your-luck gameplay, I highly recommend this one.  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Clank is a push-your-luck, ascension-style deckbuilding game where you have a few resources to manage: health, clank, money, attack, movement, and purchase power. Players will be traversing a point-to-point map using movement points from their deck. Moving from point-to-point may require a key or sword if you don't want to take damage. Along the way you'll come across merchants, randomized face-down tokens, and artifacts. Artifacts are the main purpose of the dungeon delving. If a player managers to get an artifact and get back out of the dungeon, they will receive bonus points and trigger the end game. The further you go in the dungeon, the more points the artifacts are worth, but if you don't make it above ground at the end of the game, you are eliminated. Player's purchasing cards from the central deck can trigger random attacks from the dragon. At which point all clank (cubes from all players in a pooled area) are added to a bag and a number of them are drawn and placed as damage. The frequency and severity of the attacks increase as the game continues and is at a fever pitch as people escape. I definitely see the appeal of this game and why it's popular, but I'm just not a huge fan of deckbuilding games. In addition, I'd much rather play Ra for push-your-luck, given the opportunity.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
This is every bit the silly random push your luck romp I'd hoped it'd be from watching playthroughs. I feel like deck building is my favourite mechanic but I'm loathe to commit because, lets face it, all deck builders are pretty much the same. Then this comes along with a whole new bunch of considerations. The tension at the end is strong, and players really can be hoisted by their own petard if they don't invest in movement to get around. 
Player elimination triggers an end game so is actually quite fun. Stories emerge. But nothing is too serious or tense - you could play this without thinking and still have a brilliant time, or you could play tactically or strategically. Only downside really is that I want more.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
On the positive side, the clank mechanism is brilliant and works very well for creating an atmosphere of risk taking. Certain cards – usually more powerful ones -- force you to add your cubes to the dragon bag. The dragon strikes by pulling cubes from the bag (seeded with neutral black cubes and player cubes). If your cubes are pulled from the bag, you take damage. It’s not hard to die by any means. 

So the longer you run around grabbing treasure and using powerful cards, the more likely it is that you’ll die a rich man/woman – albeit in the dungeon. Just getting out is worth 20VP so you’re heavily incentivized. The cards offered some nice synergies and different ways of building your deck. So far so good. 

The downside is that there’s an awful amount of luck that may override player decisions. In my game, I was the Start Player and got off to a fast start by grabbing early bonus chits. These bonuses helped me get deep into the dungeon fairly quickly and easily (while removing them from other players). When the dragon cubes came out, I was quite lucky and never more than half wounded. I had the luxury to stop off for some extra loot grabs even though two others had exited, still avoided any wounds, and also exited for the 20VP bonus. I won by 30 points and it all felt a little too easy. Perhaps it was beginner’s luck but I didn’t see what other players could do other than hope my cubes were pulled.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Simple deckbuilding combined with a 'dungeon delve' board makes for a fairly interesting combo.

The deck building aspect is simple... really really simple and there is not much 'combo' that you can achieve and really not much to let you thin your deck and make your engine, however because of the board part of the game it doesn't actually feel like you HAVE to streamline your deck and build you engine and churn points like many other deck builders do.Here you can have a sub-optimal deck and just enjoy the experience of the delve part.

The delve part is fairly fun with multiple paths you can follow and various treasures both face up and face down for you to acquire, but with every stolen treasure the dragon guarding it gets more and more pissed off.

The 'Clank' mechanic (noise your adventures make) is really interesting as it adds a new variable to try to mitigate, do you try to creep slowly and quietly round the dungeon, or do you stock up on healing items and stomp around in your heavy (noisy) plate armour.

Its a little off towards the end when players are no longer buying from the river of cards thus there is less dragon attacks, but a simple house rules could fix this thematic break

RATING: 7.7
Slotted insert holds sleeved cards!  Thank goodness, another savvy publisher!  

Not sure why this is called Clank (didn't see the instructions). It is a dungeon, but no one in chains....yet, I guess if you make any noise (clanks) the dragon hears you???  Even though I love deck building games, this one looks bland to me...tiny cubes, a meeple, a board that doesn't grab my attention.  As the rules were explained, I thought this is just a copycat Ascension with so many similarities, and then I thought too, Adventurers Pyramid of Horus when players try to make it out of the pyramid, after finding hidden treasurers and backpacks to carry more.  And like Shogun, cubes go in, and blind, some come out to deliver damage.  Hmmm.  Boring.  Nothing new.  But.....I changed my mind!

Even though I found the "Clank" coming randomly out of the bag made the game quite unpredictable and difficult to follow a plan. & unfair!!!---it also made the game quite fun, especially when rooting for the demise of others!  

The outstanding board design with the movement thereon, is the gem and new element in this game.  The board offers many options with different avenues for movement, so even with a thwarted game plan(s), numerous other choices still make victory possible.  The board is 2-sided, offering variety.  Many cards have a unique concept... bonuses, but slapping you with the evil Clank as well.

Despite the fact I find the components lacking, and the game so reminiscent of other games, and planning so chaotic, I really like this game.  

My impression boils down to, it's fun.

Played  2 games now, and one objection to this game, not enough cards or ways to cull junk from hand.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Der Dungeon Crawler gehört zu den am meisten strapazierten Klischees je näher sich ein Spiel in Kampfrichtung Trash und Ameristrash bewegt. Parallel dazu wird es oft horrorfigürlich -  Miniaturen und Kampfsysteme ersetzen Strukturen. Manchmal verirren sich Dungeon und Fantasy in Eurogebiete wie im raffinierten DUNGEON PETZ oder wie in BLOOD RAGE. In KLONG wird der Dungeon von einem Drachen beherrscht, der den Raub von Artefakten durch uns Helden verhindern soll und durch die lauten Klongs aus dem Schlaf gerissen und alarmiert wird. Die Miniatur ist hier noch ein liebevoll geschnitzter Holzmeeple und die Schadensmarker sind Ressourcenwürfel euroklassicher Abstraktion. Daran lässt sich erkennen, das KLONG mehr sein will als sein Thema, auch wenn die Karten, die man sich in sein stetig breiter werdendes Deck sammelt, von Fantasyklischees nur so wimmeln wie ein Wimmelbild. Ja, auch Deckbau als Hipster-Mechanismus findet in KLONG seine Verwendung und macht es zu einem vergnüglichen Abenteuerspiel flacherer Einflugschneise ohne dabei an Varianz einzubüssen. Klingt widersprüchlich, ist aber schön. Diverse spielerische Wege führen durch das unterirdische Labyrinth im Erdreich unter dem natürlich dunklen Schloss. KLONG ist ein Konsensspiel, welches das spielende Gros gerne wieder mitspielt. Das Ganze in den Weltraum zu verschieben scheint mir übrigens eine sehr gute Idee zu sein, um aus Fantasy mehr Phantasie zu machen. KLONG IN SPACE darf angeflogen kommen. Vermutlich wie auch hoffentlich als Deutsche Adaption beim Schwerkraft Verlag, auch wenn der VK-Preis wie bei KLONG im Lachhaften bleiben wird. Trash as Trash can.

RATING: 10
This is my favorite game. When I first saw it, I wasn't sure I would like it. The board looks a bit fiddly, and looks like a confusing maze. But the deck building mechanic and the games hype  was enough to give it a try! I'm so glad I did, because once you play you understand the board and it makes sense why it is laid out that way. It no longer bothers me. 
This games core is a deck builder that generates movement as a resource during your turn, in addition to money and things. With your movement you move around the board and are on an adventure. It has a ton of unique cards and high replayability. It also has a push your luck element where you can buy cardd that make noise (a bad thing) for sweet bonuses. It even comes with two distinct boards, one on each side. 
It plays well with two or four, but three is my favorite. 
I'm almost ready for the expansion and clank in space, but I'm still enjoying the original so much it will be a while until get them.
P.s. there are two cards called "tattle" in the market that make you add clank ("noise") on your opponets. We decided to throw these cards away, because we are all friends and the flavor was off with rattling each other out. Theives honor!

RATING: 10
Clank is a fun, engaging game!  It is a deck-builder, dungeon crawl which is light/medium weight and is done in an hour or so even with new players.  You cannot plan too far in advance since you don't yet know what will be available to pick up for your deck.  In between turns, you need to watch the strategies of the other players to make sure you have enough time to execute your plan, and also watch to see if "Nicki" wakes up to try to roast you!  

The instructions are straight forward and easy to follow, and can be covered in less than 10 minutes.  

I am very glad I bought this game, and would recommend it highly to regular and casual board gamers alike!

RATING: 8
Although I'm not a huge fan of deck-builders, I believe this will supplant Dominion as my favorite in the genre.  Even though it is very luck dependant, I love the dungeon delving aspect of the game.

It's in the style of Ascension with a random market of 6 cards available at any one time instead of all cards being available at the same time (like in Dominion).  I like that this makes setup and cleanup easier, but it becomes more tactical since often times the card that you want to buy is no longer there when it's your turn. 

Sometimes you just get lucky and the right card at the right time shows up in the market. Like when you teleport into a locked room (with no key) to snag the high point artifact before you opponent can, and now you're stuck until your teleport card comes back around.  Oh look that Teleporter device just showed up in market right before my turn - neato!

Situations like that is what makes me love this game.  The dungeon delving along with deck building really hits on all cylinders for me.  True, sometimes you go on a long streak of bad luck and there's nothing you can do, but it is still a blast to play.

RATING: 7
Surprisingly enjoyable deck building game.  Am not really an adventure game player, but can be tempted now and again, especially with a low play time of about 60 minute.

Good production value.  Some folks have reported issues with missing components, but their customer service appears to be great (had the components for the yellow player.. twice.  Wrote to them and got a response with a few hours!).

Although you choose which card(s) to purchase and where to move, it may be a tad random, as it really depends on the cards which are available for purchase, and how the player(s) before you play, and what they buy (if anything).

Starting last is a big disadvantage, in that you really need to go in deep to get a useful artifact, and changes are players who played before you got there first, so you end up with the left overs.  When you are last, a strategy is to purchase movement cards, if the darn things are available for purchase!  :)

Reduced from an 8 to a 7 after another game where I started last and had a hard time picking up movement cards...  Ended up with a 5 point artifact and was behind the winner by 35+ points even though I was able to get out and get the +20...  When you are last, too many things need to go your way...

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.75
Clank! is a fast-moving deck-building dungeon-crawler, which pits players against the Dungeon, and paces them with a vengeful Dragon who lashes out at those stealing the treasure.
Basically, the game is DungeonQuest, or even Dungeon- but the map is far more fixed, and the penalties both more abstract, and more immediate- and much more forgiving.
Players start from a common portal into the Dungeon, and do not fight each other or help each other, except that they race towards he same treasures and secret tiles, trying to amass more than other players and still make it out alive and conscious.
There are no specialized player races or classes- so all players have the same total damage, and the same base card set.
Players hands generate three important values each turn: Movement, Combat, and Skills (money to buy cards to add to player decks) and may accumulate one penalty value, Clank!
Clank! is the innovation- collecting treasure (and victory points) or other noisy actions increase Clank!, measured in player color cubes.
Somewhat like the stacked deck in Pandemic, cards in the Dungeon deck may trigger a backlash (Dragon attack) on players- and the blind draw of Clank! cubes from a common bag allots the Dragon's retribution- and the cubes drawn become player injuries.
There is no set length of game, last player leaving the dungeon or being rendered unconscious by the increasingly irate Dragon triggers a count of Points collected- assuming the players made it either out of the dungeon entirely, or close enough the players can be saved to count their points.
The first player to leave the dungeon sets off a damage clock, forcing the game end within a few turns- this keeps things moving, and the game is generally light and enjoyable for all.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
Very interesting/different take on deck-builder. 

From friends that have played this a LOT, it seems that escaping first is actually a big gamble not in your favor. As the other players get 3 more turns before the game ends, they can spend those turns potentially buying more points/collecting stuff/etc. Also just heading towards the entrance generally signals to everyone else what your plans are (so they have more than 3 turns to prepare for the end). Also the cards that show up in the shop display can make a big difference if you get a few lucky purchases.

This is a game that is definitely played more for the fun of exploring, not for winning against other players due to skill. I don't think I would actually recommend this, but if it were on the table, I would play again.

RATING: 8
A great job of working a map into a deck-building game.

The game presents interesting choices, is _very_ thematic, easy to teach and above all is... fun.
It has potential to hit the table easily and often.

FANTASTIC replayability.  Only a portion of dungeon cards come into play each time.  And _when_ they come is critical for their usefulness.  Thus different cards/their combinations are in the spotlight each time.

This is only the second deck-builder to enter my collection (after Ascension).  The other ones failed to excite me [shrug].

--

I wonder if almost non-existent mechanics of trashing cards out of the game here is a conscious designer's choice or a blatant omission...  Maybe some of it is planned for an expansion :>

EDIT: 4-player mode is weak. The game is watered-down, there is no _real_ race, no _real_ tension, precise and on-the-edge planning is non-existent. The interaction is random.
I won’t be repeating this mode.

RATING: 5
2017-03-31

Initial Rating: 6.5 (March 2017)

Clank!: A Deck-Building Adventure can be a good deckbuilding game. It was much better than expected, but still it isn’t a game for me.

The rules are easy to teach. You can do it under 18 minutes. Playtime is around 90-110 minutes.

The art of the game is pretty good. The game´s components are very well done as well. The game board is prone to break. In the copy I played it was partially loose.

The idea of the game and the theme are pretty neat. You are exploring a dungeon looking for treasure while the dragon tries to kill you. The more noise you do in search of treasure, the more likely the dragon will hit you.

As most deckbuilding games, it has a high replayability factor. You don’t see all the cards in one play and the board is double sided. Also there is one expansion already out.

Clank! features a variable market offering (like Ascension, Legendary and Star Realms) and that’s a big issue for me. The luck of the draw is amplified by this and it is very unfair when a player can buy a great card in his turn and another can’t just because that card isn’t available anymore. I always prefer more fair deckbuilding games with an static market offering (Dominion, Penny Arcade, Tanto Quore). I really hate when luck alone decides what player can buy, that is, Clank is much more tactical than strategic. 

Due to the variable market offering, the game has a high luck factor and if you add the random distribution of the noise cubes (in our game the dragon hit the most the player who had the least cubes in the bag), you get an uncontrollable luck factor and that’s the main reason I sold the game, it is unfair and I cannot stand this kind of deckbuilding game.

The bonus tokens add another layer of uncontrollable luck and it seems they are very situational, sometimes they are very powerful, other times very weak. To summarize, the luck factor is very high and uncontrollable. 

The game decisions aren’t not that interesting, but, thanks to the map, they aren’t that obvious either. The map allows you to strategize a bit and plan ahead. It has some element of push your luck seeing how long can you remain in the dungeon.

Best with 3 fast players, with more, the downtime is excessive for such a simple game.

Another issue I have with the game, when a player exits the dungeon, the game continues for four whole turns, every other player can play four additional turns and that’s way too much of an advantage, even if someone dies in the upper part of the dungeon. I feel this part is unbalanced, you can do much more than 20 points in 4 turns.

Bottom line, Clank!: A Deck-Building Adventure can be a good deckbuilding game for some players, but not for me, it is very unfair and luck plays a prominent role. It is a, mainly, tactical endeavor and you have to react most of the time. The planning you can do is very restricted and due to this I vastly prefer to play Dominion (a game in which I can plan all my game from the very beginning). Perhaps it is the best deckbuilding game that features a variable market offering out there, but still it isn’t enough for me to keep it. I already sold my copy of the game. I would play again if requested but if I don’t play it again I won’t be sad. The game´s idea is pretty neat though but its execution is disappointing for me.

Current Rating: 5,0

RATING: 7
Neat idea, and doesn't overstay its welcome - with the caveat that at least one of the players is trying to make sure that people aren't overstaying their welcome; the game can bog down significantly if players become too involved in plumbing the depths of the dungeon. When played at a brisk pace though, it becomes a tighter affair as you race to get the best treasure you can before turning around and hauling yourself back out before time runs out. It then becomes a risk/reward situation where delaying escape for a round or two can outweigh the bonus at the dungeon's exit. The addition of the push-your-luck element helps raise Clank! beyond its deckbuilding peers; you're still at the mercy of what random five cards you'll have on your turn. But you've got the option to focus on those dangerous/powerful/valuable cards to strike quickly and get back out of the dungeon as fast as possible.

RATING: 10
Nov 2016
This sooo fires Dungeon! and a few other crawlers out there. It almost fires Dominion and some other deck-builders out there too. Have played 2 2-player games and had a blast. Scored 103 pts the first time and a miserable 61 pts the second. Had a great time both games. It starts slow and just speeds up from there. The deck building aspect is very clever and the display has cards that affect the game while they remain in the display. So you want to get rid of them asap if you can. There are instants in the display too, as well as cards that you can buy and add to your deck. The artwork is fabulous and the board outstanding; double-sided for easier and harder. 
It's great to start combo-ing your hand of cards together. Sometimes starting with 5 and building up to 8 or 10 cards even. Brilliant variety of cards to keep the game interesting. Lots of D&D-style cards to choose from - Elven Cloak, Teleporter, Wands, Boots of Swiftness, Pickaxe, Gems, Dragons Eye, etc, etc. It's great fun checking out all the different stuff you can buy.
Your deck can 'stall' at times if you don't have enough boot symbols on your cards; no boots, no movement. I died in the second game near the dungeon entrance as I drew 3 hands with only 1 boot of movement.
Awesome fun! A must buy. This should charge into the Top 20 if not the Top 10.

RATING: 8
I won't say this is my favorite deck builder but it might be the one I have the most fun playing. I'm still coming to grips with exactly what that means.

I like that's it's competitive without being too cutthroat. It's possible to adversely affect your opponent by trying to incite dragon attacks or by snatching loot out from under their noses but it all seems really good-natured.

I like that there are different ways to build out your deck and so there are a number of ways to win.

It's fun to try to decide if you want to push your luck to go a little deeper or stay in the dungeon a little longer. It's very satisfying to count your loot at the end.

I've played solo a couple of times with the app. It's okay but I vastly prefer playing with other folks and there are other games I would prefer to solo.

All in all, I'd say this one was a winner and I'd happily play anytime.

RATING: N/A
I'm mostly burnt out on deck builders. Most of them seem to be basically the same game. I like clank because it adds more than just buying the cards and playing a game of who has the best 'engine'. 
The movement around the board adds more decisions to make than just 'what should I buy this turn', but doesnt add too much to be overwhelming for players new to the genre of deck building.

The dragon mechanic of drawing random cubes of who gets attacked is also a new twist on similar random damaging type of mechanics.
Again, this adds more decisions for the players of trying to self manage the amount of 'clank' you are producing.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
I am not going to describe how the game works, and I wont be explaining what I like about it either, you can find that on any other 5 starts review, I will only be listing the possible problems you might find in this game, and like I said, it is a fantastic game and it desires 9/10 IMO.

- Being e first to leave the dungeon is never in your favor, the 3 turns you miss effects you very badly, if others weren't really that far behind they will have 3 turns to catch up and leave the dungeon safely, unless they were too greedy but then it would be their own option to drop the advantage they got. In most of the games I played though the first person to leave was knocked out, so this is not a big problem, but it makes leaving on your own less of an option.

- Creating combos in Clank is very hard, if you wanted to combo +Clanks with -Clanks you will have to invest in too many "card drawing" cards and you will need more -Clanks than +, otherwise you might end up in terribly bad situations, and investing that much in one combo is not effective, so eventually it might be better for you completely forget about combos and just avoid card with so many +Clanks.

- Because combos are not that effective, focusing on a certain strategy with card purchasing isn't very impactful, you can randomly buy any card you like and you might still end up with the best score without any strategy.

- It isn't easy to guess where you stand in Clank, deciding wither you should dive deeper or just leave because you are on top is very hard, this is an extra random factor that I don't like.

Burgle your way to adventure in the deck-building board game Clank! Sneak into an angry dragon's mountain lair to steal precious artifacts. Delve deeper to find more valuable loot. Acquire cards for your deck and watch your thievish abilities grow.

Be quick and be quiet. One false step and CLANK! Each careless sound draws the attention of the dragon, and each artifact stolen increases its rage. You can enjoy your plunder only if you make it out of the depths alive!

RATING: N/A
"what sets this deckbuilder in a distinct class is the valuation of those cards. You see: you need all types of cards (nothing new there - that's just good tension in design), but the value of a card in the display I believe *changes* as play unfolds. What I need early in the game isn't what I really need later. Movement is always grand, but I really *do* need gold about midway through to obtain some room to hold another artifact or get the limited number of keys to allow efficient travel. Not to mention swords to help stop my own health from deteriorating. 

And I should say here that the race feeling is very real. The first player to 'die' (yes, you can be eliminated in this game) sets the end game in motion - only 4 more rounds and all is at an end. What's worse, however, is in those 4 final rounds, you will most certainly be at risk of dying yourself. Here is where the title drop lands: certain cards generate (as a penalty) 'clank' - represented by your colored cubes placed aside (for the moment) in a display on the board. When the dragon is riled up (determined randomly by the conveyor belt of cards), those cubes are tossed into a bag and a few are drawn back out randomly. Each cube of your color is a single hit on your health. If your health fills up, you are out of the game. If this happens while you are too deep into dungeoneering, you are out of the game - and lose as well (you are not even given the opportunity to score). Perhaps this is too brutal for some to stomach - but then again, such types would avoid DungeonQuest as well."

* Notes
+ What you need varies during the course of the game. Of course I will prefer the variety of the things you need in Race during a game. Maybe also I don't need this, as Puzzle Strike has this in part (need money sometimes, need crashes/combines later).
+ Fun to risk dying.
$ I don't like the conveyor belt mechanism?
+ Nice tension 
- Quite light

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.2
What's Great:
This game is very easy to pick up, but has varying strategies to extend its longevity. Adding a board to deckbuilding was truly innovative, it feels more substantial than with just cards. Short runtime allows for multiple playthroughs (and you'll definitely want to!).

What's Not So Great:
Certain players can shorten the game considerably by grabbing a quick artifact and leaving the dungeon immediately (can be remedied by house rules). The thrill of the game comes from the anticipation of new cards to purchase. Once you've seen all of the cards a few times, the thrill is gone, but strategies start to kick in at that point. 

Verdict:
One of the best (hybrid) deckbuilding games that allow both casual and competitive gamers to get into with a reasonable runtime. With the new expansion out, you'll have the option of more variety and replayability. 

We use a blind artifact house rule where all artifacts are random and face down until you pick it up. Sometimes we play a two artifact requirement variant (and the bag is just victory points) which allows for more extended play.

More tension in Tyrants, as well, since you're actively trying to maintain/take control of different areas of the map.

RATING: 6
Not a bad game, but I don't consider it to be the new standard of deckbuilding.

Much like Trains, Clank tries to merge having a board with the aspects of deck building.  Whereas Trains tries to be like Dominion with fixed stacks, Clank tries to be like Ascension with a random market line from a single deck.

Very similar to Ascension, the higher cost cards do far better than lower cost cards, and you play everything in your hand.  However, with the numerous currencies that players have to deal with (Skill, Movement, Gold, and Attack), it does make the turns a little more involved over other Ascension style games like the Legendary series.

My big issue with the game is the board barely plays a role and the balance is out of whack.  In my game, I grabbed the second highest artifact and a few treasures, was first to make it out, and still lost by half.

The player who won didn't even have an Artifact and simply stacked Ancient Tomes (victory cards similar to Dominion), gold, and had a Wizard to boost his victory points from the Ancient Tomes.  He barely played the board and won by nearly double the point.  He didn't even get the bonus for leaving since he was knocked out in the castle

Because of this, I can't see myself playing the game often enough to warrant a purchase.  Much like Trains, Clank suffers an issue where players can simply stack victory point cards to win the game without doing much on the board.  Maybe an expansion will fix it, which is a shame because they definitely have a great system at work here.

RATING: 4
Was so excited when I went to play this, but ended up so disappointed with the actual play. Issues:

1) Just too luck-based. e.g. person with fewest clank could still have most damage (by a factor of two!), and person with most clank in bag could not be damaged at all for first half of game (and never have to worry about it all game). This is the central mechanism of the game, so I was disappointed how pointless it was to try and modify clank when luck overrode all efforts here.
[Untested idea for how it could be made less random: whoever has most clank outside bag takes one guaranteed damage before cubes are put in bag (multiple people get 1 damage if tied at >1 clank outside); any remaining damage/draws are dealt randomly.]

2) Really really too luck-based: cards that are bought on the turn they appear was a real issue. Some cards are super-valuable and priced cheaply. Some cards clearly dominated others (e.g. better abilities and cheaper). This was an obvious balance issue; before the game the winner had told us to look out for 3-4 valuable cards, and almost all of them appeared on that one person's turn. Indeed, our final rankings were perfectly ordered by how many of these cards we got.
[Untested idea: Other players given option to outbid for just-revealed cards, or some other balancing mechanism to ensure price is somewhat proportionate to value.]

3) Runaway leader: Once you have a great deck (thanks to #2 above), you'll continue to build a better deck since you have more actions and skills every round. It was dead obvious who was going to win about 30 minutes in (they had more VPs, better mobility, and double actions per turn; the gap would increase by about 5 VPs each round!), and having to keep playing when you know the result is not at all fun. Especially when their lead felt more given to them (by #1 and #2) than by superior play.

:(

RATING: 6
This rating is based on only one play, something I try to avoid, but because this game does something I dislike in the extreme, I think it valid. 

I don't like deckbuilders in general, and specifically not of the Ascension variety. However, Clank manages to be fairly entertaining. I found the theme strong, and the mechanisms sound. 

Where Clank went off the rails for me was in two spots. One, it has player elimination. Two, the end game is just terrible, as the first player to leave the dungeon is out of the game, watching other players take turns. To me, that is a poor excuse for game design in what is otherwise a fairly engaging experience.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I really want to love Clank! but I find myself hesitant to give it a full endorsement.  First, the dragon mechanic in the game is too simple with 2-3 players.  The only time I feel any tension with the dragon is when we play 4 player.  Otherwise it feels like you can stay in the dungeon as long as you want and there is no real threat of a fiery death.  

Second, I wish the strategy was better.  My play group sort of discovered early that most games can be won by simply rushing to the earliest treasure, and then rushing out of the dungeon as fast as possible.  Everyone else is left to fight over the remaining items, and hope they can get out in time before they instantly die.  Once in a while someone does, but it's kinda rare.  

Finally, I find the deck building to be very uninspired.  To be honest, I've won several games by simply drafting only Explore cards with a couple other minor fillers.  It just feels like most of the cards are completely unnecessary and actually slow you down instead of help you.  

I would be interested in other people's opinions on these 3 points, because it seems that a lot of people really love this game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
[b][COLOR=#66CC33]Pro:[/COLOR][/b]  I do like the theme of going into a dragon's den and stealing his treasure. I think it shows the theme rather well since you're trying to sneak around, but you're constantly making noise and the more treasures that are stolen the more the dragon is angered. 

[b][COLOR=#66CC33]Pro:[/COLOR][/b]  This game, to generalize, is a long push your luck game. I actually like push your luck game quite a bit because of the excitement they can generate. I think that this mechanic works really well in this game because, not only do you have to make a decision on if you want to keep digging for better treasure, but you also have to determine how close you're willing to get to death. You can get cards that won't heal you, and you can ignore the small question mark tiles that may have a potion, but that may come back to bite you.

[b][COLOR=#66CC33]Pro:[/COLOR][/b]  Although the artwork isn't as good as some other card games that really put a lot into making their artwork thematic, I like the way the art in this game looks. The treasures are generally on pedestals. Each of the characters on the action cards are in the same area, which would usually be a flaw, but it almost makes this deck-builder feel a bit more like a video game.

[b][COLOR=#66CC33]Pro:[/COLOR][/b]  The game will probably last you about 45 minutes to an hour, which is the perfect length for this kind of game. Enough time to make the push your luck somewhat of a dedication and therefore more exciting, but not so long that the push your luck element could eliminate a player and have them sitting around twiddling their thumbs for a majority of the night.

[b][COLOR=#FF0033]Con:[/COLOR][/b] Some of the cards are really interesting, but I will admit they're very typical of this kind of game. I don't really know what actions these cards could've given that would subvert that "typical" feeling I get from them, but basically every card in this game is something that anybody could've easily come up with if they were to design this game. That isn't necessarily a huge flaw, because these cards still make for a fun game, but I never thought that any of them were incredibly unique or interesting.

[b][COLOR=#FF0033]Con:[/COLOR][/b] Sometimes, just by luck of the draw, the dragon rarely ever attacks. If he's always attacking, I'm okay with that because it makes the game really intense. But when he never attacks, it makes the game kinda boring. Most deckbuilders I've played don't suffer from this same problem, since it's usually what the players play that makes the difference, but never drawing dragon cards is the kind of thing that's exclusive to this game.

[i][COLOR=#33CCFF]Final thoughts:[/COLOR]       I think it's okay. Because of the push your luck enjoyment that this game can produce, I rate it higher than I otherwise would have, but there are certainly flaws to consider with this game.             [/i]
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I would call Clank! an 'advanced filler'. Rules are not too complicated, decisions are often rather easy and there is not a huge amount of strategy to be aware of. It is very thematic and can be very tense with the increasing strength of the dragon attacks and the push-your-luck mechanism when one player makes a run for the exit. Still, luck plays quite a role: drawing good card combos from your deck, having good cards available to purchase, finding helpful treasures etc. In addition, downtime between turns can be quite significant when the other players take their time weighing their options as there is almost no player interaction. Hence, the sweet spot seems to be 3 players while 2 also works ok. Not so great with 4. Plus, turn order seems to be important with players moving first having an advantage. 
Overall, gameplay does not seem to be all that different from game to game which does not bode well for Clank's staying power.

RATING: 6.5
Fast playing, fairly light deck-builder -  you are not going to see very many complex decisions in terms of what cards to purchase for your deck or even what order to play your cards in, because it doesn't really matter for the most part.  And as if deck building itself wasn't random enough, Clank adds even more luck through random bonus tiles, random cube draws.

What saves this from being an utter piece of garbage and what makes it actually fun to play is that there is a physical board through which you move your character.  The game has a push your luck element which  adds to the excitement -   Do you spend the time to gather more points and treasure or is the Dragon nipping at your heels and about to kill you, so now it is time to flee?  

The game is light enough that younger gamers and casual gamers should be able to handle it.  It is a little too long to be considered a filler.

 I did not try it solitaire so I cannot say how well it plays with only one person.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
[b]Clank[/b] 

[COLOR=#FF0000]A year later... thoughts and rating (8 -> [b]10[/b]):[/COLOR]

[i]After my initial burst of plays I was actually down on the game and only my kids' enjoyment kept me from trading it. As I continued to play I realized just how fun Clank is and it has become my favorite deck builder alongside Tyrants of the Underdark. Personally I wasn't a fan of what I'd call 1st generation deck builders where deck building was the whole game. I've really been enjoying the new deck builders that are coming out, where deck building is combined with other game mechanics. 

Getting back to the merits of Clank; number one is variety and replayability. The card diversity changes how games play out and strategies you can explore. There is more going on that first appears, but all of the card variety is layered on a very simple set of rules making Clank a breeze to teach. Also after a few plays we realized how dangerous ignoring the dragon and your clank can be. The threat of the dragon is certainly real, the more we've played the more reckless we've gotten which has resulted in a lot of death. 

Clank has definitely stood the test of time and has probably crept into my personal top 10 games [i](definitely my top 20)[/i]. Clank is a great next step family game and has been popular with gamers as well which is no small feat. I am very curious to see what Clank In Space brings to the table.[/i]

[COLOR=#FF0000]Initial thoughts and rating (6/8):[/COLOR]

[i]This has been a huge surprise hit for me because I've played a lot of deck builders that I just don't like (many of them I'm in the minority on... like Dominion). What Clank does is similar to another deck builder I really like (Super Motherload) which is use deck building as one mechanic in the game. Clank also introduces the idea of moving throughout a dungeon collecting loot while also worrying about the amount of noise you make. Noise equals clank cubes going on the board and eventually into a bag when the dragon attacks. 

All of these mechanics lead to a very quick and exciting game where you are always deciding just how far you want to push your luck, will greed get the best of you? You can die in this game which may seem like a terrible idea to some gamers, but when that happens it triggers the final few rounds of the game when the dragon starts rampaging through the dungeon, attacking at will. While there isn't any direct conflict with other players, you really need to pay attention to other players movement because as soon as someone decides to book it out of the dungeon you know time is running short.

I think this game will appeal to a lot of gamers, it's definitely great for families. The rules are easy to teach, everything you do in the game is very intuitive and turns are quick. I'd definitely recommend checking out Clank especially if you play a lot of games with kids.[/i]
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
規則:
*寶藏標記開著放對應數字位置(2/3人時先隨機移除2/1個)，大秘密跟小祕密蓋著洗勻放在對應位置(小祕密的位置一次放兩個)，沒使用的移除，市場物品放市場，猴子雕像放對應位置，專家標記使用玩家數目放圖板旁，龍標記2/3/4人分別放在龍軌第3/2/1格，24個黑色標記丟袋中，鬼怪/傭兵/探險者/秘密圖騰卡牌分別疊起放一旁，地窖牌100張洗勻開六張(如果開到有龍攻擊的開新的取代，然後洗回去)
*每個玩家拿一個顏色的30個標記，拿同顏色米寶放左上起始點，跟10張起始手牌洗勻抽五張，隨機起始，照順位放3-2-1-0個標記到右上的聲響區
*玩家輪流進行，直到所有人倒下或逃出，每個玩家回合有四個階段
1.出牌  要打出所有手牌，連動的卡牌不管打牌順序都會有效果，之後所有手牌丟到個人棄牌區
>左上藍色數字是技能點數，可用來買右下有藍色數字的牌，紫色牌買完啟動後就棄掉，其他買到的牌放到個人棄牌區
>劍用來攻擊怪物，擊敗的怪物丟到公用棄牌區並拿取獎勵，鬼怪不會棄掉永遠可打，且一回合可以打多次
>到市場時可以花錢買物品，每個都是七元
>靴子代表可以移動，正常可移動到相鄰一格，目標有兩靴代表要兩個靴子才能進去，有怪物的通道經過會扣上面數字的血量，每個攻擊符號可以少扣一滴，有鎖的要有鑰匙才能通過，有箭頭的只能照箭頭方向，每次到達房間最多只能拿一樣東西，可不拿(大小秘密或寶物)，到達水晶洞窟位置此回合不能再用靴子移動
*如果通過怪物房扣血，則從自己供應區的標記放到下方血量區標示之，補血時拿回，沒標記放聲響區可不放
>獲得錢 就拿對應錢
>聲響 放對應數量標記在右上聲響區，如果有減的，則從上面移除，也可減少當回合要放的，但不能減袋中的
*拿到寶藏或是龍蛋時要移動龍標記右移一格，寶藏身上上限1，每個背包可多拿一
2.標記  地窖牌補到六張，只要一張有龍攻擊，先把聲響區的標記丟袋中，在從袋中抽龍所在位置數目的標記數，玩家顏色的就放到對應玩家的傷害區，黑色的放一旁
*如果血量到底，且在圖板下半區則直接輸掉，如果身上有寶藏且在上半區則會被村民拯救，可進行最後計分，身上有寶藏才能逃出，如果成功逃出拿一個專家標記價值20分
*當第一個玩家逃出或被擊倒時放他的米寶到倒數區，每次輪到他時就左移一格並執行一次龍攻擊(且會加要抽的數量，最後一格所有未逃出的直接擊倒)
*遊戲有逃出的玩家加總寶藏數字，每一圓一分，還有自己卡牌內的綠色數字分數，分數最高的贏
****備註****
*獲得能力只有拿到該卡時啟動，卡牌下方到達能力則為該牌第一次到開牌區時作用，在龍攻擊前啟動，危險卡則在龍攻擊時多抽一標記，棄牌能力該牌不啟動，移除牌則移出遊戲(可從棄牌或手牌移)，溫泉補一滴血，傳送可無視規則移動到相鄰格

RATING: N/A
Competitive Ascension-style deckbuilder with a map. Each player is a hero, delving in a dungeon. There is a big push-your-luck aspect where you try to get the best relic you can, but then escape alive. After one player escapes, the others are likely to take damage every turn until they get out as well. 

Out of 100 cards, there are 2 that hurt everyone else when played, and a few more that hurt everyone when bought. That seems minor enough not to be a problem. There is also some opportunity for hate-drafting, but at least it will cost you to do so. 

Overall, it looks like one that might be fun to play. Not one I want to buy, partly due to the full-size box.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Clank! is a deck-building game that revolves around moving your pawn around a dungeon board and grabbing as much loot as you can. Cards are available to be bought through an Ascension-style continuous offer. Some cards force you to Clank, meaning you put a cube in a bag, and when a dragon card enters the offer, a certain number of cubes is drawn, and those players take a wound. Once a player's HP is exhausted, the player is either eliminated or loses out on a big bonus, depending on how deep a player is in the dungeon. Players can also leave the dungeon, which accelerates the dragon attacks and thus introduces a push-your-luck element to the game. While the deck-building aspect felt very much like Ascension, the board play was very unique and interesting for a deck-building game. On the whole, this was a fun little romp.

(1 play)

RATING: 5
Enthusiastically received by many, I felt there were few interesting decisions to be made and the 'no-brainer' cards were eagerly snapped up. I was disappointed by the deck-building aspect which has not evolved from Ascension (or Dominion, really - 9 years!): in fact it had gone backwards with the paucity of Trashing (1 card in two games).* Worse, in some respects, not getting to play with your cool cards was something I'd've hoped to not see again after playing Baseball Highlights where your newly acquired card goes onto your deck, not into your discard. That all sounds more negative than I feel, but expectations will do that to you. It's OK, would prefer some rule/card tweaks.

*If the designers were worried about people trashing Clank cards - and so breaking the central threat mechanism - just say 'Trash a non-Clank'; or, have a Minion Character that runs off (Trashes itself at the same time) with a card from your hand, or an On Acquire power that just triggers once. To be playing with a handful of complete crud at the end of the game is, if not ridiculous, very annoying.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Pros:
1. Integrated Board - This is the first deck builder where the board felt like an essential piece of the game.
2. Variability - There are a ton of cards with lots of interesting things to do.
3. Fun - This game is just flat out a good time. Collecting treasure, fighting monsters, all while pushing you luck.
4. Luck - There is just the right amount of luck in this game to keep it interesting. New players can pull of the win, but experienced players have more advantages.

Cons:
1. Variability - While I also consider this a strength, the large variability in the cards make it nearly impossible to build cool combos.
2. Theme and Mechanics are Disjointed - This is always an issue with a deck builder. Your deck consists of actions, and items, companions. So, it's not clear what your deck actually represents. I'd consider this a rather minor problem.

Summary: This is a great deck building game. All around just love this game. Great artwork, clean mechanics, and fun to play. Highly recommend purchasing this game.

RATING: 7
A have a very mixed feeling about Clank! When it works, it is a wonderful experience, you are all laughing, mocking those who are in a bad situation or praying for the right cards or are standing just before the exit of the dungeon with and praying for a lucky draw from the dragon bag. 
It is a game about stories to tell: once I have teleported into a closed room without a key knowing that the only way out will present itself only after I redraw the exact same card. Another time (with the first expansion) I laughed in a scuba gear as my friend reached a treasure underwater without a scuba gear just to die a horrible suffocating death like the bad guys in a B category Indiana Jones movie.
But thenn there are those games, where there is no tension, really, just like yesterday. Actually at the end of the game the bag was empty, all but one players escaped and all felt it was the most boring game we played in a while....
Which is the true face of Clank!? I have to play more to find it out...

RATING: 8
This is the game DungeonQuest should have been. The deck-bulding provides a good chunk of decision making, along with the ability to carve your own path through the dungeon. Clank cubes, representing noise/danger, create a real sense of impending doom. =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
I have cooled on Clank since my initial plays, but to me, it remains a commendable entry in the deck-builder genre. Its system is streamlined and intuitive enough that even non-gamers can soon grasp the object of play, while still providing novel synergies for gamers to find satisfaction in the gameplay. The theme is rather generic, but alas, tried and true, and serves to fit the game very well. The fun-factor can wane over too frequent of plays, and of course you are subject to the whim of the clank cube draw. The game does provide a handful of ways to mitigate clank, and regardless of what people may complain about, managing your clank cubes really does make a significant impact. Overall, this is a solid medium-level filler game, though I fear it, and its "sequel", will likely be eclipsed someday. 

(+) Streamlined deck-building gameplay.
(+) Retains a race-like feeling by presenting treasure acquisition on a first-dibs basis and the risk of losing it all by overstaying your welcome.
(+) Accessible to non-gamers and provides crunchy decisions for those more strategically oriented.

(-) Generic fantasy trope theme.
(-) Luck plays a large role (can be mitigated)
(-) Does not offer much variety (in deck-building choices or depth of gameplay) after several plays.
