RATING: 5
Played this at GenCon 2016. The game plays almost exactly like Ascension with a board movement component. There are several resources you gain from cards, movement, fight, and purchasing power. The victory condition is whoever has the most 'treasure' at the end of the game. Simply escaping from the dungeon gives you 20 bonus coins.

I felt this game could be fun for a couple play through, but suffered from being to reliant on luck during the early game, the late game then greatly favors whoever got lucky at the beginning. Once you get 'behind' it felt like there was very little I could do to catch up.

In the end I felt like this was a game that didn't do anything novel or interesting enough on its own to justify purchasing it.

RATING: 6

Like every other deckbuilding game with a board that I've played, I felt like the board was an unnecessary complication and that I would have preferred a game that was contained entirely within the deck of cards, likely using some to track state in a way distinct from just being shuffled into your deck.

RATING: N/A
Pre-ordered from Funagain 8/23/2016. $35.99. Arrived 12/6/2016.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
Ascension meets RPG elements is essentially what Clank boils down to. But, it does it in such a refreshing deck-building way that everyone who plays this game that I've played with enjoyed the game, and the replay-ability.

What makes clank different? It's a dungeon-crawling deck builder. In most deck builders you can go heavy into one strategy, and usually expect to accumulate a lot of points with that, but Clank takes a different approach. You actually have to BALANCE your point generating cards with things like MOVEMENT and COMBAT, and perhaps even HEALING or else you will score 0. Yes, there's a way for you to score absolutely nothing, and that in my opinion is amazing.

The game offers many different strategies, and FORCES you to adapt to the trade row. Do you usually like to go for the larger point artifacts? Great! But what if not many movement/gold generating cards appear in the trade row? Gotta switch it out! I love that fact.

Disregard comments about: "This is all about luck" or "There is no flavor to this game" or "This doesn't add anything new." That's completely ludicrous. Positive reviews generally explain what is great about the game, and while negative reviews can offer constructive criticism, it's usually hypocritical when you look at their "favorite games" and see a purely luck based game, or a bland game in their library. Clearly, they missed the point.

That being said, the only reason I gave this review an 8.5 instead of a 10 is because I feel like they could have certainly added more depth to the cards. Don't get me wrong, the variety/mechanics of the game are splendid and solid, but I feel like there could have been more interesting mechanics with the cards you acquire. That being said, an 8.5 means I love this game and would still recommend it, just I have other games I probably would prefer over it.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
It's Ascension with a game board.    No seriously, that's EXACTLY what this is.

However, it's the board that makes all the difference.  Maneuvering around the board on your quest to score points adds a dimension of depth that Ascension has tried (and largely failed) to accomplish.   Further, it establishes a far more cohesive theme and the feeling that you are actually competing against the other players, rather than the players each playing solitaire at the same table that you get with Ascension.

The unpredictability of the dragon attacks adds a fun dimension of excitement as well.  It is random, of course, but exactly the right level of random to add fun to the game without making it feel like your play is completely at the mercy of the fates.

If there is one drawback it is that the points aren't quite balanced right.  With the current point weights, there is no incentive to get any artifact beyond the cheap ones near the surface and beeline to the exit.    (I understand this has been addressed in Clank! In! Space! but this review isn't about that game.)
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Nagyon ötletes az a mechanizmus is, hogy ha valaki kiér, akkor még gyorsabban ébredezik a sárkány és sietni kell a többieknek is, mert ha lent maradnak végük. A játék időben is pontosan megfelelően gyors. Nehéz fogást találnom rajta, hirtelen csak a szerencsét tudom hozni, a zsákból húzás miatt, de nem zavart annyira. Ami jobban zavart, hogy az alapjátékban és az első kiegben is nagyon kevés olyan lap van, amivel csökkenthetjük a paklink méretét, pedig ez egy fontos elem a deckbuilding világában.
Ettől függetlenül nagyon tetszett.

RATING: N/A
Played this a couple of times at CastleCon and really enjoyed many aspects of this ... It is a deck builder, of course, but also a race game - trying to race into the dungeon and grab more treasures than anyone else before the dragon devours you.  
The race itself though presents choices ... The paths in the Dungeon are maze like in that there are numerous ways to get through them ... and the first out of the dungeon starts a game wind-down mechanic.  

You can make an effort to obtain a key so you can take shortcuts or hopefully buy a flying carpet ... or run like hell trying to move as fast as possible ... hopefully drawing "swords" when you need them to defeat monsters in the tunnels ... 

You can only grab one of the main treasures so do you grab one worth 5 pts near the entrance or go deeper to attempt to grab one worth 25 or 30 points.  Everyone else is making the same decisions as they race through the place ...

RATING: 9
This is a deck-building adventure/race game.  I remember there was a lot of love for Trains when it first came out because it was a deck building game with a board.  I personally wasn't that impressed with Trains but this game takes that deck builder with a board conceit and does it much much better.  Along with improving your deck by getting skill points and using those to purchase cards you also collect movement and combat points to move around a dungeon map and fight monsters.  Many of the spaces on the map have special properties and the main goal of the game is to collect a valuable artifact and make it out of the dungeon.

The namesake comes from the fact that many actions in this game make "Clank" or more simply put, noise.  This is represented by colored cubes matching your player color which are put into a big bag and occasionally the dragon attacks by pulling cubes from the bag and the noisiest players are more likely to be attacked.

This is what I was hoping to get out of Trains, I like deck builders and I love the idea of another gameplay layer on top of it.  This plays so quickly and has a lot of variability.  I came in last place my first time playing it but I was one movement point from coming in first.  I pressed my luck to get more points and ALMOST made it out.  Those kind of butt clenching moments that could make or break you are part of what makes a great game.

I can't help but be a little disappointed by the quality.  The cards and art are fine but everything is cardboard or cubes past that.  There are so many amazing looking games that have come out over the past couple years that maybe I'm just a little spoiled.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

The board has two sides so it adds some variety by offering two different dungeons to explore. I'm not sure about long term replayability though.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.8
tl;dr: fun, light deckbuilder

This is a mixture between [thing=36218][/thing] and an adventure game. The deck building is very standard but it does use a mix of fixed cards and a moving row of available cards. Also: some cards are not bought but defeated (like in [thing=53953][/thing]).
The adventure part has you go in a dungeon, encountering obstacles, finding valuable items and making sure that you make it out on time.
There is a big luck factor in what items you turn over. If you're looking for a certain type of item and you never turn it over, tough luck.
While you play your cards, you might make noise, this makes the dragon angry, and he might hurt you because of it. So managing the amount of noise you make is an important part of the game.
This is quite enjoyable, but it is very light. This is not a deep strategic game.

Initial rating: 6

RATING: 8
Ranking at the top of current board games that I play with my lovely girlfriend is Clank!  For much of its (usual) 60—75 minute duration, this game is a point salad free for all, but this 360 degree scramble is given some direction in that the board is a dungeon delver and there are a limited number of gettable items.  Add to this a simple deck building mechanism that multiplies possibilities and creates a puzzle, and the resultant game is a unique and fun conflation.  And then there’s that very fun (and ominous) press-your-luck titular mechanic with the dragon bag, from which cubes (wounds) are drawn.

Overall, Clank! is easy to learn and a lot of lighthearted fun....but once somebody exits the dungeon, the countdown to death begins, and the pressure and intensity increase immediately.  Kind of like Mage Knight (simplified) meets Super Mario Brothers in a subterranean Candyland.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
The deck building is a bit simpler and more complex than Dominion: fewer cards available, but every card might come out. Like Trains, Clank has unlimited actions and buys, and additionally unlimited fights. You also get coins (you buy with "influence") to use in store spaces in the dungeon. (Clank refers to noise you make that disturbs the dragon.) You win by getting out with the most points; you lose by dying.

RATING: 7.5
Clank applies a unique theme to the deckbuilding-with-a-board genre currently occupied by games like Trains and Automobiles.  I think the theme in this is great.  You are adventurers delving underground, trying to get as much loot as possible and get back to the ground surface.  The dragon attacks people with growing ferocity, and the target of his attack is based on how much noise (or "clank") you make while running around.

The deck building is pretty good.  There are 4 currencies: skill (like gold in Dominion), feet (which let you move through the dungeon), gold (primarily worth VPs), and swords.  The swords let you move through monsters without taking damage, or you can "kill" some cards in the market to get rewards.  The game uses the Ascension/Star Realms-style market of 6 random cards, although they do not immediately replace.  I generally prefer that Dominion-style market, but I think the random market works well here.  It works because some cards cause dragon attacks when revealed and some cards do other effects when revealed.  Something like that wouldn't work with the Dominion-style.

Movement on the board is pretty interesting.  There are a lot of paths to choose and those whole thing is one giant exercise in push-your-luck.  You can buy items like keys (for locked doors) and backpacks (to hold more treasure).  There are also exploration tiles that give you random bonuses, and get stronger as you go deeper.

Overall, the game comes together nicely.  There is a lot of luck, but it feels fitting with the theme and push-your-luck element.  In my first game I tried to sprint and grab a treasure, then get out and leave everyone to get eaten.  I ended up making so much noise that I died to random dragon attacks on the turn before I was about to make it back to the castle.  At least you still get points when you die, you just don't get the bonus points.  I'd like to try it a few more times to explore different strategies. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
Good thing about games that copy elements from Dominion is that it can be easily taught to players familiar with the Dominion concept.
Biggest difference probably lies in the fact that the effects of your cards played doesn't depend on in which order you played the cards, thus I had a slight feeling of flying in autopilot. That being said, what you buy really makes your deck and offers a much bigger basic variance in contrast to your average Dominion, where everyone adds cards from a choice of ten card piles to his deck. In Clank, every round offers you new options to alter your deck in completely different ways. Deckbuilding spiced up with elements of Push-your-luck is a very enjoyable mixture. At least, in this case it is!

RATING: 5
Pound for pound, there are better deck builders out there.... In terms of perfected design, Clank falls short of titles like Dominion, Vikings Gone Wild, and Hero Realms where the game chose an idea an executed it stunningly, Clank falls noticeably short. Now that said, where Clank excels (enough to match scores, in Dominions case in my mind) is that while it lacks the same polish in what it does, it does some things that are really deeply original and fun. Similar to how Legendary is frankly a mess compared to some other deck builders but still has a place with the best of them because of how in touch it is with its theming and the fun metamarratjve components that come with that and it's shear versatility in scenarios, Clank's card pool is lacking in both size and complexity... There's no factions or subtypes and cross card synergies are minimal. Things can feel slow with a bad hand while the best hands don't elicit the excitement they might in other games, and ultimately has some issues of polish... What it DOES have is a totally novel feature in its favor, that not only is your hand simulating you vs dungeon (not the more common PVP or players vs Villain/s), but that the board and it's many features. The noise mechanic for simulating dragon aggro is in particular a brilliant reconciliation of RNG and strategy it's easy to see why they titled the greater game after it. There are enough complications, optio
ns, rewards, and mechanics on the board to make a game all on its own, combined with adeckbuilder, and any shortcomings are forgivable for the "Quality" of a more unique take on the genre. Definitely a must play for Deckbuilder fans.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
First play impression: Just pure fun. The main mechanic is simply Ascension and similar games, so you only need to learn a few rules about how the board works as long as you're already familiar with that style of deckbuilder. This means you can jump right in and start running around the dungeon even on your first time playing without being bogged down with rules.

It does seem like getting certain good cards early on can have a big impact on the game. I was able to remove both of my starting clank cards early in the game, but none of the other players had a chance to cull their deck just because the right cards never came up on their turns. However, this can happen in most deckbuilders and I'll need to play more to see how significant the luck factor is.

Update: I still stand by this game being fun, but after more plays it does seem like the randomness is pretty significant. There are very few cards that let you thin your deck or draw more cards, so you're left to the luck of the draw and it's hard to pull off any sort of card-specific combos. The cards that you can buy add another layer of randomness. Sometimes the perfect cards come up for a player and you watch them pull off a huge combo. Then on your turn there is nothing but low-value junk. I put this game into a category along with Mystic Vale, Star/Hero Realms, Jump Drive, and a few other games: they're lots of fun to play, but the luck of the draw is a deciding factor so they're not to be taken too seriously.

RATING: 8.25

Clank! offers a fun blend of deckbuilding, push-your-luck, and exploration. You don't cycle your deck often enough to reap the rewards of much synergy but there is an arc to your dekcbuilding, starting with inexpensive cards that allow you to combat small monsters or explore further and leading to cards that clog your deck but offer many victory points.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Clank! is a deckbuilder with an actual board. The game has three types of currency: movement, skill (spend) and fight. The object of the game is to run into the castle/dungeon, grab as many points as you can and get safely back out.

You start with some cards that give you skill and movement, and of course, two 'Stumble' cards which add "Clank", noise. Whenever you make noise, you have to put one of your cubes on the board. Eventually the dragon will attack. At that point you put all those cubes on the board into the bag and draw cubes.

The bag starts with a bunch of neutral cubes, which generally aren't replaced, and any cubes that aren't drawn stay in the bag for subsequent rounds. The angrier the dragon gets the more cubes you draw for his attack. He gets angrier over the course of the game. Cubes represent damage to players. When your cubes are drawn you put them on your health track. If that fills up, you die. And lose. Well... technically if you make it out of the dungeon you don't lose, but you don't get a bonus for getting out safely.

Inside the castle there are many paths to follow. Moving requires spending movement, but there's all sorts of impediments to moving, like crystal caverns where you have to stop moving, paths that require you to fight a moster or take damage, paths that require keys, etc.

For some reason, there's a market in the dungeon. Don't ask. If you are at the market you can buy keys, backpacks and crowns there. There's also artifacts strewn around the dungeon, ranging in value from 5 to 30. Unless you have a backpack, you can only carry a single artifact... and you can never drop an artifact, so pick wisely.

There's a few cards that are always available to buy and a card display that replenishes at the end of each turn. There's all sorts of things you can buy to specialize your character.

Once any player dies or leaves the game, a clock starts and you only have a handful of turns to get out of the castle. Players who do that can get a bonus 20 points.

I enjoyed the game. It's got the "deckbuilder problem" that you can get randomly hosed if you draw things at the wrong times. That's a bit more painful given that there's more game here. There's also a random draw from the bag which can, and was, painfully random. Despite most players having roughly the same number of cubes put into the bag over the course of the game, when we checked the final distribution, one player only had 3 of their cubes left in the bag, out of 30 total cubes. Which meant that their cubes had been drawn a lot more often than other people's. Unsurprisingly, they died. It's still a relatively short game, so it's not the end of the world, but it is still a little annoying.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
Managed to play Clank at PAX West 2016 before its release. It's a really fun game, most similar to Tyrants of the Underdark. A deck builder with dungeon exploration and a very fast learn. The only flaw is that players can be eliminated randomly and quickly, and they have to sit out and watch the entire rest of the game without participation. 

What's worse, the press your luck element goes a little bit too far and says that players that die on the bottom half of the map have a score of ZERO at the end of the game, and thus already automatically know they lost, so they don't even have interest in the end result of the game.

I'd like to see a fan-made module to add or an expansion that allows dead players to interact with the game in a meaningful way. I'd also like to see this module provide a path for deceased players to be able to win the game, even if that path is more difficult and unlikely.

RATING: 7
Clank! is sort of Dungeon Quest fixed, via a deck building mechanism. Players are trying to explore a deadly dungeon, grab an expensive artifact and then escape before the dungeon's deadly dragon awakens and kills them.

As far as deck-builders go, this is completely by the numbers. If you have played any deck-builder before, you probably already know how to play this. Turn structure is play and resolve action cards, add up the gold and then buy new cards. Draw up to hand limit and then do it again.

What is different, is the map component. Your cards will generate three stats...movement, combat and clank. Movement pushes your pawn across the map. Combat kills any monsters you run across and clank puts one of your cubes into the noise pool. What's a noise pool? One of the coolest parts of the game.

Whenever the dragon awakes (typically through a card reveal in the market, about a third of the cards will trigger an awakening) all the cubes in the noise box go into a bag. Then a few are pulled out and every cube pulled that matches your color results in one damage. s the game goes on and the dragon gets angrier, more cubes are pulled in each attack.

Eventually someone will decide they have pushed their luck enough and it is time to break for the surface. As soon as that happens, the race is on. Every turn after the first player exits the dungeon, the dragon attacks escalate and draw more and more cubes from the bag. It is incredibly tense and in my experience thus far, every card draw becomes a piece of high drama after someone gets out.

If you are too deep and don't find the surface before you run out of hit points, you die.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
An evolved deck builder fantasy dungeon crawl using pouch pulling and point to point movement.  It is evolved in that the cards indicate more than the traditional buy points and combat points.  In addition, cards in a hand determine whether you make noise "clank" in the dungeon and when the guardian dragon attacks and how fast you delve.  The dungeon board is a maze of different paths leading to different rewards depending on the luck of the draw and how you build your deck.  The end game thematically incorporates a clever race of being chased to the surface by an increasingly pissed off dragon.

RATING: 6.7
Minimal player interaction.  A handful of cards cause minor harm to other players, and there are enough spaces on the board that you can't really block someone else from completing the mission.

Very difficult to set up a good deck.  The available cards to purchase are randomized (shuffled) before the game.  Even if you manage to purchase  cards from a single faction, the card synergies hardly provide any benefit.  Decks feel like you end up with a random assortment of cards and just hope you draw enough that are useful each hand.

It's not a bad game, but it could have been better.  The deck building is pretty weak, and the board play isn't substantial enough to pick up the slack.

RATING: 6.5
I haven't given a half-star rating in years, but this one earns it.

There's a real sense of dungeoneering in Clank!, and the noise/rage/dragon mechanic is a blast. It's just too easy for an imminent loser (or smart aleck) to snatch an artifact, race to the exit, and prematurely end the fun.  Perhaps the "advanced" board fixes this issue?

I will say that, of all the deck- and bag-building games with boards (Trains, Automobiles, Hyperborea, Tyrants of the Underdark, A Few Acres of Snow, etc.), this is my favorite.

I do wish that Clank's board were less onerous to set up.  Sometimes you just want to sit down and play, and not waste time with extensive pre-game prep.  But if everyone pitches in, I suppose Clank's chit chores aren't too severe.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I like the deck building aspect of the game. More games should employ this feature. My critique of the game is the fact that there is a limited strategy to the game which limits the game's replay ability. You are limited to only two "game boards".  From several plays, owing to the way the game boards are laid out, there is a clear strategy to winning.  The game board should have been designed in a way that it was interchangeable with multiple different tiles for each level of the dungeon. This would have prevented a set strategy from evolving when playing the game. Currently the way it is designed is that the deeper one goes the greater the reward. This fact leads many players to not go for the deeper reward, but instead they go for the 20 point marker and then get out quickly to earn the twenty point bonus for escaping plus whatever they pick up along the way. The person going for the thirty has a much tougher chance of winning. this leads to a sameness in the game's strategy. There has also been a suggestion that the artifacts should also be set and hidden at random like the major and minor secrets. A slight design change that includes a randomized board with hidden artifacts would have made this game much better. An optional screw your buddy element would have also made the game more challenging. Games are conflict for a winner, so I do not understand people who do not like games with conflict, but the screw you buddy cards could be optional. Maybe even a RPG element like Talisman to it would make the game go even further.

RATING: 10
I love this game!

I really like deck-building games, but many of them (Dominion for example) can become "solved" for players with more experience. For a given set of available cards the "obvious best strategy" isn't obvious to the newer players and all the fun drains out of the game for everybody.

Clank's has a wider diversity of cards, and their availability throughout the game is random, so you wind up with the field being a bit more level for players of different experience levels.

I have friends that like "Fun" games, and friends that like more technical games, and this seems to satisfy both camps. I've only played Clank! three times, but I fully intend to pick up a copy of this game the second it becomes available.

RATING: 5
In my  opinion, the game is enjoyable if played as a family game, but hard gamer should agree that Clank is completely out of control. Random cards available every round, random damage cube drawn from the bag, random Secrets tokens and just disadvantages to begin the game as the last player.
This is not a deckbuilding game, players have almost no control on their decks: you just buy cards that may be useful. There is no way you can build a combo: you have to buy the (at least) two right cards (or buy the first and then pray to see the other one in future rounds) and then hope you’ll draw them together! Yes, hope, because just one or two players will be able to buy something that will allow them to remove cards in their deck (in my opinion, the only thing that allow the perfect deckbuilding).

I really can’t understand those who call Clank “a good deckbuilding game”. This is a good push your luck game, a very good family game, a good game to play in just one hour, not a good deckbuilding game. No way.
If you want to play a good deckbuilding game, try Thunderstone, Rune Age or, at least, Dominion.
